  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5eddf488-d2ee-4521-a64f-595fd9ba9a57'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer2179967188447490045">In two full-length plays--Millennium Approaches and Perestroika--Kushner tells the story of a handful of people trying to make sense of the world. Prior is a man living with AIDS whose lover Louis has left him and become involved with Joe, an ex-Mormon and political conservative whose wife, Harper, is slowly having a nervous breakdown. These stories are contrasted with tha</span>
  <span id="freeText2179967188447490045" style="display:none">In two full-length plays--Millennium Approaches and Perestroika--Kushner tells the story of a handful of people trying to make sense of the world. Prior is a man living with AIDS whose lover Louis has left him and become involved with Joe, an ex-Mormon and political conservative whose wife, Harper, is slowly having a nervous breakdown. These stories are contrasted with that of Roy Cohn (a fictional re-creation of the infamous American conservative ideologue who died of AIDS in 1986) and his attempts to remain in the closet while trying to find some sort of personal salvation in his beliefs.</span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/97039-emma"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1502092437i/97039._UY100_CR1,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/97039-emma">Emma</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Depends on what triggers the love. <br/>If the frivolous gayness attracts, then maybe 'The Adventures of Priscilla, Queen of the Desert' would be something<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Depends on what triggers the love. <br />If the frivolous gayness attracts, then maybe 'The Adventures of Priscilla, Queen of the Desert' would be something you could like. Or 'Flawless' with Robert de Niro. If OTOH it's the quick wit, the smart repartee you appreciate, you may enjoy the writings of Aaron Sorkin, like 'The American President' or 'The West Wing'.<br />Unfortunately, I haven't found anything that combines the two, and adds angels to the mix to boot. <br />If anyone does know of such a work, I would be interested to know about that title too. :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer13683651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4444714813960666881">"Night flight to San Francisco; chase the moon across America. God, it’s been years since I was on a plane. When we hit 35,000 feet we’ll have reached the tropopause, the great belt of calm air, as close as I’ll ever get to the ozone. I dreamed we were there. The plane leapt the tropopause, the safe air, and attained the outer rim, the ozone, which was ragged and torn, patches of it threadbare as old cheesecloth, and that was frightening. But I saw something that only I could see because of my a</span>
  <span id="freeText4444714813960666881" style="display:none">"Night flight to San Francisco; chase the moon across America. God, it’s been years since I was on a plane. When we hit 35,000 feet we’ll have reached the tropopause, the great belt of calm air, as close as I’ll ever get to the ozone. I dreamed we were there. The plane leapt the tropopause, the safe air, and attained the outer rim, the ozone, which was ragged and torn, patches of it threadbare as old cheesecloth, and that was frightening. But I saw something that only I could see because of my astonishing ability to see such things: Souls were rising, from the earth far below, souls of the dead, of people who had perished, from famine, from war, from the plague, and they floated up, like skydivers in reverse, limbs all akimbo, wheeling and spinning. And the souls of these departed joined hands, clasped ankles, and formed a web, a great net of souls, and the souls were three-atom oxygen molecules of the stuff of ozone, and the outer rim absorbed them and was repaired. Nothing’s lost forever. In this world, there’s a kind of painful progress. Longing for what we’ve left behind, and dreaming ahead. At least I think that’s so." wow.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4444714813960666881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848426313" href="/book/show/34993151-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=gay-rights">gay-rights</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=gay-fiction">gay-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3068697077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17768995544699048742">I've never seen this play performed in person, but reading it in print was still a powerful experience. The AIDS crisis of the 1980's hit when my parents were teenagers, so I don't really remember it, but I think <i>Angels in America</i> really captures it in a way that can be universal to anyone. It is hard in a world with such differing, polarized views on politics, religion, sexuality and gender, to create a story that can have something for everyone and address it all at once. <i>Angels in America</i> doe</span>
  <span id="freeText17768995544699048742" style="display:none">I've never seen this play performed in person, but reading it in print was still a powerful experience. The AIDS crisis of the 1980's hit when my parents were teenagers, so I don't really remember it, but I think <i>Angels in America</i> really captures it in a way that can be universal to anyone. It is hard in a world with such differing, polarized views on politics, religion, sexuality and gender, to create a story that can have something for everyone and address it all at once. <i>Angels in America</i> does it very well.<br /><br />Sometimes quite humorous but ultimately tragic and deeply thought-provoking, I think this is definitely one of the best contemporary plays I've ever read, although personally I imagine it would be much more impressive to actually see performed live on-stage. It's one of those books that just needs to have a visual accompaniment.</span>

<div id="review_2319878028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2319878028" />
    <a title="Sketchbook" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4708498-sketchbook"><img alt="Sketchbook" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296491148p2/4708498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2319878028?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sketchbook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sketchbook" href="/user/show/4708498-sketchbook">Sketchbook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2319878028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6671065820618545073">Kushner's overheated - and vastly overrated - opus sent me scurrying for my Yma Sumac CD, "The Voice of the Xtaby." When I want a guest to leave my apartment, I put it on with the admonition, "You must hear her 5-octave pipes!" and, shortly, I am happily alone. You too can hear Yma on YT. She trills from high soprano to basso. The music suggests tweeting birds or a volcanic eruption. Kushner, I read, thought his play might be a musical, initially, and it would have needed Yma. It still does. <br/><br/>Its</span>
  <span id="freeText6671065820618545073" style="display:none">Kushner's overheated - and vastly overrated - opus sent me scurrying for my Yma Sumac CD, "The Voice of the Xtaby." When I want a guest to leave my apartment, I put it on with the admonition, "You must hear her 5-octave pipes!" and, shortly, I am happily alone. You too can hear Yma on YT. She trills from high soprano to basso. The music suggests tweeting birds or a volcanic eruption. Kushner, I read, thought his play might be a musical, initially, and it would have needed Yma. It still does. <br /><br />Its success is a prime example of how a few mediocre dramer critics, infected w toxic fairy dust or nerve gas, can stampede the public into casting off sane reflection and start belching cheerless huzzahs. Kushner's "monumental achievement" mixes gays and Jews and Mormons (huhh?) in a series of blackout sketches, performed by usually two characters (I dont think he can write for 3 actors onstage). The AIDS crise turned him into a Writer, as it did others, so attention must be paid, as Arthur Miller rumbled. Since Kushner has <i> nothing to say,</i> he deals solely with emotions: mostly agitation and anger. A young man dying of AIDS is abandoned by his lover who becomes involved with a closeted gay Mormon who, in turn, has a shrill, pill-addicted wife. The monstrous lawyer Roy Cohn, also dying, gets a ghostly visit from the pathetic Ethel Rosenberg; amid the hysteria, and juvenile raillery, an angel descends and --- where's Yma Sumac?<br /><br />Like Brecht, Kushner does not write "characters." He writes "symbols" : Evil, Affectation, Death, The Oppressed. His jabber goes on endlessly. "Our suffering teaches us solidarity; or it should," he allows. "Because Kushner has written a second-rate play...about being gay, and about AIDS, no one is going to call [it] the overwrought, coarse, posturing, formulaic mess that it is," explains a writer in the New Republic. Meantime, essayist Andrew Sullivan, who loathed the play, dismissed it as political agitprop, adding: "Gay life - and gay death - surely awaits something grander and subtler than this."<br /><br />I saw an early preview c 1991, and the ranting and raging onstage put me to sleep, though I awoke when Roy Cohn (Evil) was dying in pain, which made members of the audience feel Good. I tried to see the Mike Nichols movie, and again I got the snores, especially when Meryl Streep appeared as a rabbi (or was that a bad dream?) It took me a few days to finish a play read, w long naps. The frenzy and yelping agony of <i>passion</i> in Kushner's revue sent me to Yma Sumac, the Peruvian songbird. Skip this theatrical salacacabia and give yourself up to Yma.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6671065820618545073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1561207259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1561207259" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25213052-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443734293p2/25213052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1561207259?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/25213052-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781854599827" href="/book/show/1067905.Angels_in_America">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25213052-nathan?shelf=four-and-a-half-stars">four-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25213052-nathan?shelf=pulitzer-booker-nba-winner">pulitzer-booker-nba-winner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25213052-nathan?shelf=poetry-and-drama">poetry-and-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25213052-nathan?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1561207259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6408131981432929060">I don't know if this play had its intended effects on me; because I was born in the 90s, HIV/AIDS has always been a reality permanently etched in the back of my mind. Because my political views lean heavily to the left, I find the recent trend of Reagan worshipping revolting. Because I live in the epicenter of Mormondom, I can poke holes in the "Mormons are the new Jews" motif that Kushner loves exploring so much. The sudden shifts Kushner is trying to articulate and rationalize have been a part</span>
  <span id="freeText6408131981432929060" style="display:none">I don't know if this play had its intended effects on me; because I was born in the 90s, HIV/AIDS has always been a reality permanently etched in the back of my mind. Because my political views lean heavily to the left, I find the recent trend of Reagan worshipping revolting. Because I live in the epicenter of Mormondom, I can poke holes in the "Mormons are the new Jews" motif that Kushner loves exploring so much. The sudden shifts Kushner is trying to articulate and rationalize have been a part of my life since birth, so there's really no way I can get into the right mindset when reading his work. <br /><br />But if literature was defined solely by its ability to achieve its desired outcome, it would be infinitely duller. While the political nightmare described in <i>Angels in America</i> is still all too real, the human reality is what aches through the entire play. Kushner writes of a world apathetic to its outsiders dying alone. He writes of feeling alienated, defeated and abused in ways that will always be relevant. Early on, Prior replies to Harper's fears of Joe's infidelity that: "I would say 'fuck the truth', but usually the truth fucks you", which carried my mind through the entire play. This is a story of people trying to igonre the fact that their ideals are shattered, only to be ruined because of it. <br /><br />This would have probably gotten a fifth star from me(even with that awful ending) if I hadn't read Kushner's "Notes About Political Theater" at the same time, an essay which made me aware of the play's shortcomings. Kushner writes that his goal in being a playwright is to make people aware that "[w]e are less able to see the political: in life, as in art, much energy is devoted toward blurring the political meaning of events, or even that events <i>have</i> political meaning", which I have trouble finding in <i>Angels</i>. Before reading the essay, I saw the play as a small step in the right direction; it's much more difficult to get the average person wanting to dismantle heterosexist standards if they can see the good in the people those standards knock down. And Kushner's play makes itself remarkable for refusing to make people with HIV/AIDS disgusting or dirty. And yet he refuses to go any further than that. The nuclear family is constantly affirmed. Even though it exists in Belize and Louis, no form of intersectional queer identity is never explored to its full potential. And Roy's death upholds a positivist attitude that bad people are the only ones swallowed up by illness and pain. It's disappointing. Had Kushner turned up the heat it would have been a much more worthwhile exploration. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6408131981432929060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2538020754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2538020754" />
    <a title="ALLEN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58158333-allen"><img alt="ALLEN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578421145p2/58158333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2538020754?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ALLEN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ALLEN" href="/user/show/58158333-allen">ALLEN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781559363846" href="/book/show/9828349-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2538020754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10052179022339346427">This review is of the two plays by Tony Kushner housed under the title ANGELS IN AMERICA: A GAY FANTASIA ON NATIONAL THEMES -- "Millennium Approaches" and "Perestrokia -- which can be produced and mounted individually, or together for one rather long (seven-hour) afternoon and evening in the theater. <br/><br/>Although the two plays were workshopped in 1990 and played jointly on Broadway and the West End in 1992 and 1993 -- they are really about the Eighties. Set in 1985 and 1986, with an Epilog in 1990, </span>
  <span id="freeText10052179022339346427" style="display:none">This review is of the two plays by Tony Kushner housed under the title ANGELS IN AMERICA: A GAY FANTASIA ON NATIONAL THEMES -- "Millennium Approaches" and "Perestrokia -- which can be produced and mounted individually, or together for one rather long (seven-hour) afternoon and evening in the theater. <br /><br />Although the two plays were workshopped in 1990 and played jointly on Broadway and the West End in 1992 and 1993 -- they are really about the Eighties. Set in 1985 and 1986, with an Epilog in 1990, they're about a people who were credulous enough to believe that the old ways would hold if they just stayed the course. <br /><br />The first play ("Millennium Approaches") has largely to do with a gay man who falls in love with a closeted, conservative Republican Mormon who abandons his wife. This causes no small amount of confusion in gay, analytical Louis through most of both plays: <blockquote><i>"It's just that, you know, belonging to a political party that's one half religious-zealot-control-freak theocrats and one-half ego-anarchist-libertarian cowboys [shrilling for 'freedom'] . . . you've had a lot of practice straddling cognitive dissonance? Or, or what?" </i><br />from "Perestroika," Act 3 (p. 195).</blockquote> <br />On the whole, ANGELS is a freewheeling and often surreal theater piece that gives a role to the late Ethel Rosenberg, who had been executed on federal charges of espionage 32 years earlier. A major role belongs to the imperious, grey-winged Angel (played gloriously in the HBO adaptation by Emma Thompson) whom the lead gay character with AIDS, Prior, must straddle to get her attention: <i>"The body is the garden of the soul."</i> <br /><br />A major character in both plays play is the real-life Roy Cohn, a professional political opportunist who furthered the climate of "Witch-Hunting," persecuting not only political dissidents but inducing a "Lavender Scare" among gay men, during the Joseph McCarthy years of the 1950's. He, too, is homosexual but will not allow the word anywhere near him, even as he prepares to die of AIDS ("liver cancer"): <blockquote>From the play -- Roy Cohn, diagnosed with AIDS, threatens his doctor: <br /><i>"No, say it. I mean it. Say: 'Roy Cohn, you are a homosexual.' . . . And I will proceed, systematically, to destroy your reputation and your practice and your career in New York State, Henry. Which you know I can do. . . To someone who doesn't understand this, homosexual is what I am because I sleep with men, but this is wrong. Homosexuals are not men who sleep with other men. Homosexuals are men who, in 15 years of trying, can't get a pissant anti-discrimination bill through City Council. They are men who know nobody, and who nobody knows. Now, Henry, does that sound like me?" </i><br />from "Millennium Approaches," Scene 9 (p. 195).</blockquote><br />[Reviewer's Note: The real Roy Cohn once "treated" a reporter to a limousine-ride interview while simultaneously cooling his anal warts (contracted just as you think they were) with an air-conditioner vent. Not for nothing did playwright Kushner call the Eighties "the Fifties in drag."] <br /><br />Tony Kushner has given us two plays that are probably among the best and certainly among the most powerful of late-Twentieth-Century American theater. If you like plays and how they are written, this volume belongs in your home. Also well worth having is HBO's 2005 miniseries adaptation with top-notch actors like Meryl Streep playing Ethel Rosenberg and Al Pacino as Roy Cohn, which I have reviewed at Amazon.<br /><br />from the play: <i>"You may be dumber than shit but I refuse to believe you can't figure it out. Try."</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10052179022339346427" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2055418114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2055418114" />
    <a title="Emma Getz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64276445-emma-getz"><img alt="Emma Getz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539752632p2/64276445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2055418114?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Getz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Getz" href="/user/show/64276445-emma-getz">Emma Getz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64276445-emma-getz?shelf=read-for-a-class">read-for-a-class</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64276445-emma-getz?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64276445-emma-getz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/64276445-emma-getz?shelf=favorite-plays">favorite-plays</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055418114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8555194602763196332"><blockquote> "This disease will be the end of many of us, but not nearly all, and the dead will be commemorated and will struggle on with the living, and we are not going away. We won't die secret deaths anymore. The world only spins forward. We will be citizens. The time has come." </blockquote><br/><br/>Angels in America is my favorite and absolutely the most beautiful play I have ever read for many, many reasons. First and foremost, it is a real look at a historical era and crisis so often erased in popular media. The inclusio</span>
  <span id="freeText8555194602763196332" style="display:none"><blockquote> "This disease will be the end of many of us, but not nearly all, and the dead will be commemorated and will struggle on with the living, and we are not going away. We won't die secret deaths anymore. The world only spins forward. We will be citizens. The time has come." </blockquote><br /><br />Angels in America is my favorite and absolutely the most beautiful play I have ever read for many, many reasons. First and foremost, it is a real look at a historical era and crisis so often erased in popular media. The inclusion of real historical figures like Roy Cohn and Ethel Rosenberg only grounded this even more. At the same time, the play exists in the realm of magical realism, for lack of a better term. It pushes the boundaries between real and fantasy but grounds it in religion, truth, and life. Each character is incredibly complex and dynamic, so there are no antagonists in this story, apart from the nature of the Reagan era and AIDS itself. The dialogue is clever and humorous while being incredibly raw and heartfelt. It is heartbreaking and uplifting at the same time. The scenes are ingeniously and masterfully crafted and staged. Overall, it is a masterpiece of both theatre and literature. If I were to choose a play that EVERYONE should read, it would be this one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8555194602763196332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104765258-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573252975p2/104765258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3159390968?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/104765258-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104765258-david?shelf=plays">plays</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3159390968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16099610601304789815">Everyone's life in this play is/becomes affected by AIDS. The time is 1985. It is a scary time with AZT brand new. As Prior Walter's fever culminates, his talks with Angels and some others from the next world intensify. The effect of AIDS does not care how strong a character may be in their earthly life. This play displays a variety of different personalities and how they handle AIDS as it crosses their path. A fast moving play with short scenes. Even in these short scenes, there may be two sequ</span>
  <span id="freeText16099610601304789815" style="display:none">Everyone's life in this play is/becomes affected by AIDS. The time is 1985. It is a scary time with AZT brand new. As Prior Walter's fever culminates, his talks with Angels and some others from the next world intensify. The effect of AIDS does not care how strong a character may be in their earthly life. This play displays a variety of different personalities and how they handle AIDS as it crosses their path. A fast moving play with short scenes. Even in these short scenes, there may be two sequences and dialogues going on simultaneously (hospital room; at home). There are some connections between characters revealed early. More interesting connections develop as the play goes on.<br /><br />I am sure I would like this more as a Live performance. The stage directions are written into the play (overlapping dialogues, sound queues, pauses, etc.) There were consistent small monologues (multiple sentences) by characters that would not be done so much in normal conversations. These messages were important, and were part of the personality of this play.<br /><br />At no point did I know how the play would end, until it ended. While not a 'surprise' ending, it is still one you must wait for. That is a sign of a story that keeps you paying attention and wanting to read (or watch) even more.<br /><br />Angel: "He wants to live."<br />Prior: "Yes. I'm thirty years old, for God sake. (soft rumble) I haven't done anything yet, I... I want to be healthy again. And this plague, it should stop. In me and everywhere. Make it go away."<br />Angel: Oh We have tried. We suffer with You but We do not know. We Do not know how."<br /><br />Solid 4.5, but I don't feel the need to buy this book, so I round down.<br /><br />Great ending quote in the epilogue:<br /><br />"We won't die secret deaths anymore. <br />The World only spins forward.<br />We will be Citizens. <br />The time has come."</span>
  <a data-text-id="16099610601304789815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_118828778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118828778" />
    <a title="Jamie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1118970-jamie"><img alt="Jamie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512217497p2/1118970.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118828778?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamie" href="/user/show/1118970-jamie">Jamie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1118970-jamie?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1118970-jamie?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118828778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11480368125666753079">I begin this review with a quote: "Things fall apart / the center cannot hold." A colleague pointed out the resonances of Yeats' poem 'The Second Coming' in Kushner's 'Angels,' and I had to agree with his fantastic observation. This is a drama set in Reaganite America that images a world seemingly coming to an implosive and horrifying end. God has literally abandoned us (evidently, during the great San Francisco earthquake), and the national and historical crises alluded to--the onset of the AID</span>
  <span id="freeText11480368125666753079" style="display:none">I begin this review with a quote: "Things fall apart / the center cannot hold." A colleague pointed out the resonances of Yeats' poem 'The Second Coming' in Kushner's 'Angels,' and I had to agree with his fantastic observation. This is a drama set in Reaganite America that images a world seemingly coming to an implosive and horrifying end. God has literally abandoned us (evidently, during the great San Francisco earthquake), and the national and historical crises alluded to--the onset of the AIDS epidemic being the most present, but also the fall of the Soviet Union, the infection of Reagan-era individualism, the legacy of the Cold War, the Rosenberg trial--profoundly intersect with the personal crises that provide the play's sometimes overwhelming sense of trauma.<br /><br />Roy &amp; Prior are each wrecked by AIDS; Harper is a pill-popping agoraphobe; there are closets galore; there are pervasive narratives of abandonment (emblematized in the one committed by God) and of comings-home; of religious doubt &amp; the terror of change--with its corollary, the terror of stasis. There's also, as evidenced by figures like Harper, Joe, Louis, and Prior, the terror of being with--and being isolated from--other people. Roy Cohn is both a historical figure and a kind of literary master narrative--as my professor remarked, Roy reads almost as analogous to Milton's Satan. He's the most despicable character, ostensibly the villain of the play, but ultimately also becomes an intensely compelling one to follow. <br /><br />With all of this said, I simply have to remark that this is, first and foremost, an absolutely magnificent work of literature. It's beautifully written, refreshingly literary (without being as pretentious as I've been in this review), often laugh-out-loud hilarious, and emotionally affecting in a way I haven't experienced with a fictional work in a long time. Read it. Seriously, READ. IT. For your betterment as a human being, give the play a shot. It's just radiant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11480368125666753079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129761553" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129761553?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manda" href="/user/show/4513555-manda">Manda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4513555-manda?shelf=50-book-challenge-2011">50-book-challenge-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129761553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8075586117376564976">I absolutely love this play. It explores the beginning of the AIDS epidemic in the 80s, particularly its effect on the gay community. But you don’t have to be a gay man with AIDS living in 1985 to relate to it. This play reaches out on a very basic human level. It’s about dealing with loss, love, sickness, regret, hope, politics, betrayal, sex, religion, death, confusion, hate…it’s about facing yourself and trying to deal with what you find there.<br/><br/>Angels is hands down my favorite play. It’s writt</span>
  <span id="freeText8075586117376564976" style="display:none">I absolutely love this play. It explores the beginning of the AIDS epidemic in the 80s, particularly its effect on the gay community. But you don’t have to be a gay man with AIDS living in 1985 to relate to it. This play reaches out on a very basic human level. It’s about dealing with loss, love, sickness, regret, hope, politics, betrayal, sex, religion, death, confusion, hate…it’s about facing yourself and trying to deal with what you find there.<br /><br />Angels is hands down my favorite play. It’s written in 2 parts: Millenium Approaches and Perestroika and is somewhere around 7 hours when performed back-to-back.<br /><br />Seriously, if I could set the curriculum for a literature class, Angels in America would be top priority. I think it’s an important play and that everyone should grab a copy of it and just read the hell out of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8075586117376564976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6850408" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6850408" />
    <a title="Dusty Myers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/423999-dusty-myers"><img alt="Dusty Myers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1190841956p2/423999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6850408?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dusty Myers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dusty Myers" href="/user/show/423999-dusty-myers">Dusty Myers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6850408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11277708121276545873"><i>Angels in America</i> is seven hours long. You need to break the two parts up over the course of a weekend, probably. And it might be the first and it might be the only gay epic ever written. And this is why it's one of the most important books I've read. Luckily it's also one of the best.<br/><br/>Its project is a tough one: look at the rise of AIDS in the culture of Reagan-era New York City as experienced by three men who identify as gay, one Mormon who's oriented sexually toward other men, and Roy Cohn—who</span>
  <span id="freeText11277708121276545873" style="display:none"><i>Angels in America</i> is seven hours long. You need to break the two parts up over the course of a weekend, probably. And it might be the first and it might be the only gay epic ever written. And this is why it's one of the most important books I've read. Luckily it's also one of the best.<br /><br />Its project is a tough one: look at the rise of AIDS in the culture of Reagan-era New York City as experienced by three men who identify as gay, one Mormon who's oriented sexually toward other men, and Roy Cohn—who spent a lifetime in the closet and died in 1986 of complications due to AIDS. Introduce angels to the scene and try to humanize everyone no matter how villainous they might act. More than its length, <i>AiA</i> is magnificent for the honest way it goes about compassion. Hannah, the mother of the closeted Mormon, becomes at the end of the play a New Yorker in looks and all, amiable friends with a gaggle of gays without having gone all haggy about it. She is able to make this change because she knows herself, and her selfhood is as strong as her faith. She's in the end a kind of hero.<br /><br />I will always remember Prior's final lines, will let them ring in my head long after I've forgotten everything else. He's talking to the audience:<br /><br />"This disease will be the end of many of us, but not nearly all, and the dead will be commemorated and will struggle on with the living, and we are not going away. We won't die secret deaths anymore. The world only spins forward. We will be citizens. The time has come.<br /><br />"Bye now.<br /><br />"You are fabulous creatures, each and every one.<br /><br />"And I bless you: More Life.<br /><br />"The Great Work Begins."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11277708121276545873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2771660291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2771660291" />
    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5909003-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384045940p2/5909003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2771660291?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/5909003-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781559363846" href="/book/show/9828349-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5909003-claire?shelf=read-harder-2020">read-harder-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2771660291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2908681290222200047">I’m still a believer that plays are made to be staged and seen, not printed and read. That being said, I found Angels in America immensely affecting, and I am glad I read it. Much more than a story of the AIDS epidemic, this is a story of humanity in crisis. It asks us big questions about who we are when faced with our own mortality, and the mortality of those we love, as well as what it means to feel like you need to be someone you are not. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2008277013" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14373090660196947916">Loved this! The Roy Cohn thing was fascinating.<br/><br/>But I'm a fan of the Aristotelian unities in my theatre ... so it wasn't <i>perfect</i>. Wouldn't it have worked with fewer scenes, longer scenes, more dialogue? In the notes, the playwright talks about how the Angel only works with good SFX ... can you say a play is working if it needs good SFX? And why can you write scenes that directors can remove?<br/><br/>Loved Belize. And Meryl is fantastic in the TV show. Really ... it's through her that Part 2 works.<br/><br/><b>Joe at t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14373090660196947916" style="display:none">Loved this! Correct. That alone in the eyes of God.<br /><br />- The failure to measure up hits people very hard. From such a strong desire to be good they feel very far from goodness when they fail.<br /><br />- I try to tighten my heart into a knot, a snarl, I try to learn to live dead, just numb, but then I see someone I want, and it's like a nail, like a hot spike right through my chest, and I know I'm losing.<br /><br />Belize:<br />- Watching him stick his head up his asshole and eat his guts over some relatively minor conundrum - it was the best show in town.<br /><br />- I have to go. Pain's life.<br />- Sing it, baby.<br /><br />"Americans pay high prices for maintaining the myth of the Individual: We have no system of universal health care, we don't educate our children, we can't pass sane gun control laws, we elect presidents like Reagan"<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1024461424" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1024461424" />
    <a title="Stian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21675244-stian"><img alt="Stian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594832709p2/21675244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1024461424?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stian" href="/user/show/21675244-stian">Stian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781854599827" href="/book/show/1067905.Angels_in_America">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21675244-stian?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21675244-stian?shelf=drama-and-poetry">drama-and-poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21675244-stian?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1024461424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1534393648168622793">I find it exceptionally challenging to write about this play. Partly because I've never read anything like it before (a "Gay Fantasia on National Themes") and partly because I feel like the play is dealing with so many themes at once in such a short space that it becomes overwhelming. <br/><br/>The most explicit theme is sexuality. There are two characters in the play who are struggling to deal with the fact that they are gay. One married (with a woman) Mormon man, and another ruthless lawyer who refuses </span>
  <span id="freeText1534393648168622793" style="display:none">I find it exceptionally challenging to write about this play. Partly because I've never read anything like it before (a "Gay Fantasia on National Themes") and partly because I feel like the play is dealing with so many themes at once in such a short space that it becomes overwhelming. <br /><br />The most explicit theme is sexuality. There are two characters in the play who are struggling to deal with the fact that they are gay. One married (with a woman) Mormon man, and another ruthless lawyer who refuses to admit that he is gay, and instead labels himself as a "heterosexual man who enjoys having sex with men." There are at least three other gay characters in the play (which means most other characters), and Joe's (the Mormon's) wife, who struggles to deal with the fact that her husband is actually gay.<br /><br />It's set in 1985-1986, and AIDS is another thing the book deals with. Within the first 50 pages, two characters will have gotten the disease. Themes that naturally follow from this are things like dealing with the disease, dealing with loss; life, death, and so on and so forth. <br /><br />Another major theme is politics, and perhaps especially identity politics. There are harsh criticisms in the play of right-wing nuttery when it comes to homophobia, racism and other such bigoted things. <br /><br />A good play that I probably should re-read once my health is a bit better and my head is working optimally. To be honest, a lot of things eluded me here. The dialogue is at times strange too, and a lot of the political jabs seemed forced and unecessary. All that being said I enjoyed it and would recommend it to anyone who isn't a homophobic asshole. <br /><br />PS: My review and appreciation of the book may change in the coming weeks. I read this as part of my studies, and I will be having a lecture on this book soon. Obviously my understanding of the book will change and thus also my thoughts about it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1534393648168622793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2284180123" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2284180123" />
    <a title="Avery (Book Deviant)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33088967-avery-book-deviant"><img alt="Avery (Book Deviant)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530499661p2/33088967.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2284180123?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Avery (Book Deviant)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Avery (Book Deviant)" href="/user/show/33088967-avery-book-deviant">Avery (Book Deviant)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781559363846" href="/book/show/9828349-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33088967-avery-book-deviant?shelf=4star">4star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2284180123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer169341720074254291"><a href='https://bookdeviant.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>See more of my reviews on my blog the Book Deviant</a><br/><br/>Because this is written as a screenplay, I wasn't really sure how I would like it. It sounded really interesting, and so I decided that if I liked it, I would check out the HBO performance of it just so I can see it. I struggled with the beginning, being unfamiliar with the simplicity that a screenplay can give. But after a while, I felt more connected with the characters, despite not being able to hear their thoughts.<br/><br/>Kushner was able to convey t</span>
  <span id="freeText169341720074254291" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookdeviant.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">See more of my reviews on my blog the Book Deviant</a><br /><br />Because this is written as a screenplay, I wasn't really sure how I would like it. It sounded really interesting, and so I decided that if I liked it, I would check out the HBO performance of it just so I can see it. I struggled with the beginning, being unfamiliar with the simplicity that a screenplay can give. But after a while, I felt more connected with the characters, despite not being able to hear their thoughts.<br /><br />Kushner was able to convey thoughtful and diverse characters with just how they spoke and how they interacted with others. We got to know each separate character not by their thoughts on events, but on how they reacted to them (Lou reacting to Prior's illness, Joe reacting to Harper's addiction) and I found that very telling.<br /><br />I thought Prior's side of the story was very . . . weird? I really didn't understand the point to the Angels, nor Prior's inclusion. It just seemed like it was weird for the sake of being weird, to draw attention rather than make sense. While I really loved the story and the overall message of it, I felt like it could have been conveyed in a better way. That didn't stop me from loving the majority of the characters (but fuck Roy) and loving how they all did their part in the story.<br /><br />Final Rating: ★★★★☆<br />Overall?<br />I was pleasantly surprised with how much I liked this play, so as I write this review I'm in the middle of watching the HBO performance of it (which I highly recommend!) While I wasn't the biggest fan of the fantastical portions of this play, I really enjoyed everything else.<br /><br />I do have to say that I'm not the biggest fan of the agoraphobic rep. While I am not agoraphobic myself, I couldn't help but be a little put off from how Harper was showed to be "cr*zy" and delusional.<br /><br />Would I Recommend?<br />Yes! Although it deals with very heavy topics, I felt that there was a good balance between the heavy details and the scenes when Prior adds in a little humor.<br /><br />Trigger warning for d*ke slur, f*ggot slur, homophobia, discussion of HIV/AIDS, abandonment, addiction, homophobic parents, sexism, ableism, cheating, anti-Semitism, racism, and sex. Comment if you of any that I missed!</span>
  <a data-text-id="169341720074254291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2182376774" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2182376774" />
    <a title="Jim Dooley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20065569-jim-dooley"><img alt="Jim Dooley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367769730p2/20065569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2182376774?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Dooley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Dooley" href="/user/show/20065569-jim-dooley">Jim Dooley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20888012-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2182376774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8044520213743508956">I keep coming back to ANGELS IN AMERICA. I first saw it on tour after its Broadway opening. Originally intended to be presented on two consecutive nights, I saw the first part on a Sunday afternoon matinee, and the second part that Sunday evening. I was mesmerized.<br/> <br/>Is there a play that has been tinkered with more than this one? Having seen three productions and the HBO movie, none of them were exactly the same. Scenes were dropped, lines were added, and Angel acrobatics came and went. It is almo</span>
  <span id="freeText8044520213743508956" style="display:none">I keep coming back to ANGELS IN AMERICA. I first saw it on tour after its Broadway opening. Originally intended to be presented on two consecutive nights, I saw the first part on a Sunday afternoon matinee, and the second part that Sunday evening. I was mesmerized.<br /> <br />Is there a play that has been tinkered with more than this one? Having seen three productions and the HBO movie, none of them were exactly the same. Scenes were dropped, lines were added, and Angel acrobatics came and went. It is almost like Spielberg's CLOSE ENCOUNTERS OF THE THIRD KIND ... which version is the “official” one?<br /> <br />Regardless, it has never been less than fascinating to me. It is, indeed, a “Gay Fantasia on National themes,” but to see it only as applying to the LGBT culture is selling it short. The gay perspective is its focus. The themes it explores impacts a much broader audience.<br /> <br />As such, it is intriguing to read this today at a time when there is so much mistrust and antagonism among Americans. A core element is that forgiveness can be extremely difficult ... not acceptance or forgetting, but forgiveness. That kind of hard forgiveness must occur if Love and Justice are ever to be reconciled. And that forgiveness is not only difficult for humans. The Angels have great difficulty with it, too.<br /> <br />This edition is the last published version of the play. It does point out changes that had been made including the text of two scenes that were dropped. It also provides the production history and commentary. The strength is not only the brilliant writing, but also in exploring the human spirit when situations are unbelievably horrific.<br /> <br />I have been moved by this play every time I've seen it or read it. It is a masterwork that I highly recommend.<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8044520213743508956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2355846616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2355846616" />
    <a title="Sarah Tittle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1806730-sarah-tittle"><img alt="Sarah Tittle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1397230345p2/1806730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2355846616?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Tittle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Tittle" href="/user/show/1806730-sarah-tittle">Sarah Tittle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2355846616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18084750809064113626">I'm not normally a reader of plays, so I was surprised when I sped through this work, which in this edition is actually 2 plays along with a new introduction and some very entertaining notes about staging. This was, I believe, the first play to tackle head-on the AIDS crisis in New York City in the 1980s. I was living in NYC then, and virtually everyone I knew was touched by the disease in some way. And although homosexuality was much less accepted in that era than it is now, this play is still </span>
  <span id="freeText18084750809064113626" style="display:none">I'm not normally a reader of plays, so I was surprised when I sped through this work, which in this edition is actually 2 plays along with a new introduction and some very entertaining notes about staging. This was, I believe, the first play to tackle head-on the AIDS crisis in New York City in the 1980s. I was living in NYC then, and virtually everyone I knew was touched by the disease in some way. And although homosexuality was much less accepted in that era than it is now, this play is still incredibly powerful and relevant. As Kushner says in his 2012 introduction, "The passing years have been equally if not more confirming of the plays' . . . apocalyptic forebodings, which loom darker and resound more ominously for contemporary audiences and readers." He was writing that on the actual eve of the presidential election, which Obama won handily, but which seemed for many to crack open the fissure between the two Americas. And THAT is what this play is really about. There's so much duality here--life and death, black and white, WASP and Jew (is that a duality?) light and dark, forgiveness and guilt, love and hate. Kushner seemed to have presaged our country's divisiveness. <br /><br />In this Trumpian era, it's very enlightening to get to know the infamous Roy Cohn as a closeted homosexual screaming with his last breath that he did not have AIDS while at the same time using his power to hoard bottles of the life-saving AZT drugs. It's powerful to remember the connection between so many New Yorkers and the immigrant ancestors who escaped religious persecution to come to America. And it's also very interesting to view Mormons and Jews as having more in common than not. <br /><br />This is not a dark book, however. It is supremely hopeful. And it is really, really funny. Kushner's characters, including the angel, are so tightly drawn. There's tons of clever word play and some of the passages are super long and wordy in a Philip Roth kind of way. I saw the first play, Millennium Approaches, in the 1990s and I don't remember relishing the language as much as I did when reading this. <br /><br />Finally, both plays are being revived on Broadway right now. If you can get a ticket, go see them! But first, read the plays, so that you won't miss any word of this wondrous, hilarious, sad and hopeful masterpiece.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18084750809064113626" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2821878162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2821878162" />
    <a title="Dominic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2551271-dominic"><img alt="Dominic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578105289p2/2551271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2821878162?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dominic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dominic" href="/user/show/2551271-dominic">Dominic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780593153949" href="/book/show/44592174-angels-in-america">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551271-dominic?shelf=drama">drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2821878162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2427032260810887086">Listening to <i>Angels in America</i> with the new Broadway revival's full cast was a moving experience this week. While more reader's theater than traditional audiobook, the performances featured here, especially Andrew Garfield's Tony-award-winning turn as Prior, left me shuddering.<br/><br/>I was shocked to find out that the play's complicated and problematic but definitely repulsive villain, Roy Cohn, was not only based on the lawyer who had a hand in executing Ethel Rosenberg, but he's also was one of Donal</span>
  <span id="freeText2427032260810887086" style="display:none">Listening to <i>Angels in America</i> with the new Broadway revival's full cast was a moving experience this week. While more reader's theater than traditional audiobook, the performances featured here, especially Andrew Garfield's Tony-award-winning turn as Prior, left me shuddering.<br /><br />I was shocked to find out that the play's complicated and problematic but definitely repulsive villain, Roy Cohn, was not only based on the lawyer who had a hand in executing Ethel Rosenberg, but he's also was one of Donald Trump's lawyers and champions! Holy hell.<br /><br />I definitely recommend listening to this astonishing and bizarre story about AIDS and American shame in the 1980s, especially this new audiobook if you can't see the show, in light of today's toxic and damaging political climate. I know wrestling with my own queerness as a teen in the 1990s was shadowed darkly with a lot of shame, fear, loneliness, self-denial, even terror—all emotions this play stirs up in its literary soup, making it a heartbreaking listen. But this is a hopeful play, ultimately, about becoming citizens of the world and the responsibilities we have to others and ourselves. It has also shown me that we are all prophets to life if we only first dare to stand in our naked and vulnerable skin, even when the terrible weather of the world pelts at our bodies and tries to scare us into taking cover.<br /><br />Prior's call for *More Life!* at the 7 hour play's end is maybe the greatest two word exclamation in modern literature: "The world only spins forward. We will be citizens. The time has come. Bye now. You are fabulous creatures, each and every one. And I bless you: <i>More Life</i>. The great work begins."<br /><br />And so, The Great Work Begins.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2427032260810887086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>

</a>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+1IEIGfrK/TfzLM/EmhNtB24DwwwcB0diUX61ZpBgMzTrO5FGDCTs1ZvrXqnpAf7Ao1SU6+aNkVEbuk2FXDGSw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DZ+gcMVFarAgebeXzZ9oMEG7rgJMrVmjy3ewtwR2aAUlYUoVup7S96naqdJ4UyJ/Xo7zXdNHcvsGXKNUi0cugg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Mike Nichols\' 2003 HBO adaptation starring Meryl Streep, Mary-Louise Parker, and Al Pacino was itself a tour de force, winning 11 Emmys and introducing the play to an even wider public. This generation-defining classic continues to shock, move, and inspire viewers worldwide.\n\nNow, on the 25th anniversary of that Broadway premiere, Isaac Butler and Dan Kois offer the definitive account of Angels in America in the most fitting way possible: through oral history, nearly 200 voices in vibrant conversation and debate. The intimate storytelling of actors (including Streep, Parker, Jeffrey Wright, and Nathan Lane), directors, producers, and Kushner himself reveals the turmoil of the play\'s birth-a hard-won miracle in the face of artistic roadblocks, technical disasters, and disputes both legal and creative. And historians and critics help to situate the play in the arc of American culture, from the staunch activism of the AIDS crisis through civil-rights triumphs to our current era, whose politics are a dark echo of the Reagan \'80s. The World Only Spins Forward is both a rollicking theater saga and an uplifting testament to one of the great works of American art of the past century, from its gritty San Francisco premiere to the Butterfly was an immediate sensation when it premiered in 1988. It opens in the cramped prison cell where diplomat Rene Gallimard is being held captive by the French government--and by his own illusions. He recalls a time when Song Liling, the beautiful Chinese diva, touched him with a love as vivid, as seductive--and as elusive--as a butterfly.\n\nHow could he have known that his true love was, in fact, a spy for the Chinese government--and a man disguised as a woman? The diplomat relives the twenty-year affair from the temptation to the seduction, from its consummation to the scandal that ultimately consumed them both.\n\nM. Butterfly is one of the most compelling, explosive, and slyly humorous dramas ever to light the Broadway stage, a work of unrivaled brilliance, illuminating the conflict between men and women, the differences between East and West, racial stereotypes--and the shadows we cast around our most cherished illusions.\n\n\n\nThe original cast included John Lithgow as Gallimard and BD Wong as Song Liling. During the show\'s 777-performance run, David Dukes, Anthony Hopkins, Tony Randall, and John Rubinstein were also cast as Gallimard. Martin Sherman\'s worldwide hit play Bent took London by storm in 1979 when it was first performed by the Royal Court Theatre, with Ian McKellen as Max (a character written with the actor in mind). The play itself caused an uproar. &quot;It educated the world,&quot; Sherman explains. &quot;People knew about how the Third Reich treated Jews and, to some extent, gypsies and political prisoners. But very little had come out about their treatment of homosexuals.&quot; Gays were arrested and interned at work camps prior to the genocide of Jews, gypsies, and handicapped, and continued to be imprisoned even after the fall of the Third Reich and liberation of the camps. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17522979236161856136">Tony Kushner is an award-winning American playwright most famous for his play <i>Angels in America</i>, for which he was awarded the Pulitzer Prize. He is also co-author, along with Eric Roth, of the screenplay of the 2005 film <i>Munich</i>, which was directed by Steven Spielberg and earned Kushner (along with Roth) an Academy Award nomination for Best Adapted Screenplay.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/23685785-angels-in-america-a-gay-fantasia-on-national-themes">Quotes from Angels in America</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Harper: In your experience of the world. How do people change?<br /><br />Mormon Mother: Well it has something to do with God so it's not very nice.<br /><br />God splits the skin with a jagged thumbnail from throat to belly and then plunges a huge filthy hand in, he grabs hold of your bloody tubes and they slip to evade his grasp but he squeezes hard, he insists, he pulls and pulls till all your innards are yanked out and the pain! We can't even talk about that. And then he stuffs them back, dirty, tangled and torn. It's up to you to do the stitching. <br /><br />Harper: And then up you get. And walk around.<br /><br />Mormon Mother: Just mangled guts pretending.<br /><br />Harper: That's how people change.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/2359-harper-in-your-experience-of-the-world-how-do-people">144 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I've lived through such terrible times and there are people who live through much worse. But you see them living anyway. When they're more spirit than body, more sores than skin, when they're burned and in agony, when flies lay eggs in the corners of the eyes of their children - they live. Death usually has to take life away. I don't know if that's just the animal. I don't know if it's not braver to die, but I recognize the habit; the addiction to being alive. So we live past hope. If I can find hope anywhere, that's it, that's the best I can do. It's so much not enough. It's so inadequate. But still bless me anyway. I want more life.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/193160-i-ve-lived-through-such-terrible-times-and-there-are-people">134 likes</a>
            </nobr>
